jane eyre by charlotte bronte preface a preface to the first edition of jane eyre be unnecessary i give none this second edition demand a few word both of acknowledgment and miscellaneous remark
my thank be due in three quarter
to the public for the indulgent ear it have incline to a plain tale with few pretension
to the press for the fair field its honest suffrage have open to an obscure aspirant
to my publishers for the aid their tact their energy their practical sense and frank liberality have afford an unknown and unrecommended author
the press and the public be but vague personification for i and i must thank they in vague term but my publisher be definite so be certain generous critic who have encourage i as only large-hearted and high-minded man know how to encourage a struggle stranger to they i e to my publishers and the select reviewers i say cordially gentlemen i thank you from my heart
have thus acknowledge what i owe those who have aid and approve i i turn to another class a small one so far as i know but not therefore to be overlook
i mean the timorous or carp few who doubt the tendency of such book as jane eyre in whose eye whatever be unusual be wrong whose ear detect in each protest against bigotry that parent of crime an insult to piety that regent of god on earth
i would suggest to such doubter certain obvious distinction i would remind they of certain simple truth
conventionality be not morality
self-righteousness be not religion
to attack the first be not to assail the last
to pluck the mask from the face of the pharisee be not to lift an impious hand to the crown of thorns
these thing and deed be diametrically opposed they be as distinct as be vice from virtue
man too often confound they they should not be confound appearance should not be mistake for truth narrow human doctrine that only tend to elate and magnify a few should not be substitute for the world-redeem creed of christ
there be i repeat it a difference and it be a good and not a bad action to mark broadly and clearly the line of separation between they
the world may not like to see these idea dissever for it have be accustom to blend they find it convenient to make external show pass for sterling worth to let white-wash wall vouch for clean shrine
it may hate he who dare to scrutinise and expose to rase the gilding and show base metal under it to penetrate the sepulchre and reveal charnel relic but hate as it will it be indebted to he
ahab do not like micaiah because he never prophesy good concern he but evil probably he like the sycophant son of chenaannah well yet might ahab have escape a bloody death have he but stop his ear to flattery and open they to faithful counsel
there be a man in our own day whose word be not frame to tickle delicate ear who to my thinking come before the great one of society much as the son of imlah come before the throne king of judah and israel and who speak truth as deep with a power as prophet-like and as vital a mien as dauntless and as daring
be the satirist of vanity fair admire in high place
i cannot tell but i think if some of those amongst whom he hurl the greek fire of his sarcasm and over whom he flash the levin-brand of his denunciation be to take his warning in time they or their seed might yet escape a fatal rimoth-gilead
why have i allude to this man
i have allude to he reader because i think i see in he an intellect profounder and more unique than his contemporary have yet recognise because i regard he as the first social regenerator of the day as the very master of that working corp who would restore to rectitude the warped system of thing because i think no commentator on his writing have yet find the comparison that suit he the term which rightly characterise his talent
they say he be like field they talk of his wit humour comic power
he resemble fielding as an eagle do a vulture fielding could stoop on carrion but thackeray never do
his wit be bright his humour attractive but both bear the same relation to his serious genius that the mere lambent sheet-lightning playing under the edge of the summer-cloud do to the electric death-spark hide in its womb
finally i have allude to mr
thackeray because to he if he will accept the tribute of a total stranger i have dedicate this second edition of jane eyre currer bell
december 21 st 1847
note to the third edition i avail myself of the opportunity which a third edition of jane eyre afford i of again address a word to the public to explain that my claim to the title of novelist rest on this one work alone
if therefore the authorship of other work of fiction have be attribute to i an honour be award where it be not merit and consequently deny where it be justly due
this explanation will serve to rectify mistake which may already have be make and to prevent future error
currer bell
april 13 th 1848
chapter i there be no possibility of take a walk that day

the word in these introductory page connect themselves with the succeed vignette and give significance to the rock stand up alone in a sea of billow and spray to the broken boat strand on a desolate coast to the cold and ghastly moon glance through bar of cloud at a wreck just sink

the red-room be a square chamber very seldom sleep in i might say never indeed unless when a chance influx of visitor at gateshead hall render it necessary to turn to account all the accommodation it contain yet it be one of the large and stateliest chamber in the mansion
a bed support on massive pillar of mahogany hang with curtain of deep red damask stand out like a tabernacle in the centre the two large window with their blind always draw down be half shroud in festoon and fall of similar drapery the carpet be red the table at the foot of the bed be cover with a crimson cloth the wall be a soft fawn colour with a blush of pink in it the wardrobe the toilet-table the chair be of darkly polished old mahogany
out of these deep surrounding shade rise high and glare white the pile-up mattress and pillow of the bed spread with a snowy marseilles counterpane
scarcely less prominent be an ample cushion easy-chair near the head of the bed also white with a footstool before it and look as i think like a pale throne
this room be chill because it seldom have a fire it be silent because remote from the nursery and kitchen solemn because it be know to be so seldom enter
